```
On Mon, 11 Jul 2005 14:22:01 -0700, Scott Peterson
<scottp4.removethistoreply@mindspring.com> wrote:

>"William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.netcom.com> wrote:
>
…[14 more quoted lines elided]…
>they were in production for years.  

If you specify a status code for a file, your program had better check
it after every I-O operation for that file because the system will
blithely and correctly assume that your program is handling all error
conditions.  If you don't depending on the operation, the program will
write records to the bit bucket, use garbage left over from previous
records etc.  See your programmers reference and programmers guide for
system actions when no USE procedures and no status code is provided
for the file.  Note these comments apply to all platforms.  The
results of not doing status code checking when a status code is
specified will vary by platform and file type.
>                  
>                                          Scott Peterson
```

```
Clark Morris <cfmtech@istar.ca> wrote:

>If you specify a status code for a file, your program had better check
>it after every I-O operation for that file because the system will
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>records etc.

I'm well aware of that.  If you'd read the full thread, you would
understand that I was referring to an example that I worked on many
years ago, not recommending a good coding practice.  <g>

In that program, which were written in one of the earliest releases of
VS-COBOL, the programmer simply moved spaces to the record area in
working storage, issued the read to an ISAM file and then tested the
area for spaces.  If it wasn't, he assumed he had a successful read. I
don't advocate doing this, but these programs were in daily use for at
least 10 years at an insurance company.   

When we worked on these programs, we replaced them with proper tests,
but it wasn't easy as the programmer had used lots of little "tricks"
like that and even exploited a couple of bugs in the compiler and a
lot of what he did had problems when we tried to compile it using
later compiler versions. 



                  
                                          Scott Peterson
```

## Thread: I need a one-way encryption algorithm! — 13 msgs

### I need a one-way encryption algorithm!

- **From:** ellie.odonnell.iei8@statefarm.com
- **Date:** 2005-07-01T09:13:47-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1120234427.622603.211450@g43g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`

```
Hi,

I need to write a very simple one-way encryption alogorithm in COBOL.
It must not be able to be decrypted. I thought I could simply use the
UNSTRING function to separate all the characters in the field, convert
them to something else, and then STRING all the characters back
together into the field, but that is not working. I also thought there
was a way to count all the characters in a string, but it seems like
the COUNT verb is to count fields in a record, not individual
characters.

I have an encryption algorithm to use for numeric values, but am having
a lot of trouble figuring out what to do about the alpha character
strings.

If only there were a RANDOMIZE function for character strings!!

Please help!!

Thanks!
Ellie
```

#### ↳ Re: I need a one-way encryption algorithm!

- **From:** Arnold Trembley <arnold.trembley@worldnet.att.net>
- **Date:** 2005-07-01T16:57:03+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<zBexe.1061481$w62.882689@bgtnsc05-news.ops.worldnet.att.net>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<1120234427.622603.211450@g43g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<1120234427.622603.211450@g43g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`

```


ellie.odonnell.iei8@statefarm.com wrote:
> Hi,
> 
…[19 more quoted lines elided]…
> 

A "hashing algorithm" might do what you want.

 From Joel C. Ewing in bit.listserv.ibm-mail on March 16, 2001 (you 
can find it with google advanced newsgroup search):

"A trivial hashing function that works adequately in many cases is to 
take your data entry "key" field 4-bytes at a time, XOR these 
together, take absolute value, and then mod N' (i.e., remainder of 
division by N' - Constraining N' to a prime tends to improve the 
dispersion) and then use this..."

Of course, XOR'ing binary fields in COBOL might be a little bit 
difficult to do without a library routine or assembler subprogram.

If your function is truly trivial, you might just break up your "key" 
field into two-byte subfields, coerce each one to be a PIC S9(4) COMP 
field (I'm assuming IBM mainframe COBOL here), and simply add each 
number together, truncating the results.  The final two-byte binary 
number cannot possibly be decrypted back to the original value, and 
will give you approximately 32,767 semi-random results.

Perhaps someone else can suggest a simpler or more secure hashing 
algorithm.

I hope that helps.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: I need a one-way encryption algorithm!

- **From:** "HeyBub" <heybubNOSPAM@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2005-07-03T07:45:45-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<11cfnfkivk48g12@news.supernews.com>`
- **References:** `<1120234427.622603.211450@g43g2000cwa.googlegroups.com> <11cb9jcl7o2sv36@news.supernews.com> <da71oh$aso$1@beech.fernuni-hagen.de>`

```
Rosa Maria wrote:
> Hello HeyBub,
> if you have any solution .. please let me know ..
> thanks

The solution I've got (from the ETK Toolkit) takes a password of up to a 
bunch of characters and hashes it to a ten-digit number. It is almost 
impossible to figure out the original password - or any other word - that 
would hash to the same ten-digit number. It works like a super-dooper 
check-digit.

So, in practice, you take the defining password, hash it, and store the 
result. Subsequent attempts at a password get hashed and compared to the 
original number.

If this fits your needs, you can search for the ETK toolkit (free), or I can 
forward the whole thing.
```

#### ↳ Re: I need a one-way encryption algorithm!

- **From:** LX-i <lxi0007@netscape.net>
- **Date:** 2005-07-02T20:26:43-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<c84e3$42c73ec9$45491c57$22762@KNOLOGY.NET>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<1120234427.622603.211450@g43g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<1120234427.622603.211450@g43g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`

```
ellie.odonnell.iei8@statefarm.com wrote:
> Hi,
> 
> I need to write a very simple one-way encryption alogorithm in COBOL.
> It must not be able to be decrypted.

Whether it can be decrypted or not depends on the tenacity of the 
hacker.  Typical hashing algorithms, such as MD5, need more than 15 
characters.

However, check out "ord" intrinsic function - it gives you the character 
code of the specified character.  Once you have a number, you can 
(within reason) do some sort of bit-twisting with it, then use the 
"char" function to make this new number into a character.  Keep in mind 
that with ASCII, your character code doesn't need to be higher than 256.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: I need a one-way encryption algorithm!

- **From:** mwojcik@newsguy.com (Michael Wojcik)
- **Date:** 2005-07-03T17:18:10+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<da96ki025rl@news4.newsguy.com>`
- **References:** `<1120234427.622603.211450@g43g2000cwa.googlegroups.com> <c84e3$42c73ec9$45491c57$22762@KNOLOGY.NET>`

```

In article <c84e3$42c73ec9$45491c57$22762@KNOLOGY.NET>, LX-i <lxi0007@netscape.net> writes:
> ellie.odonnell.iei8@statefarm.com wrote:
> > 
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> characters.

The output of one-way functions like MD5 can never be "decrypted",
because they lose information - that's what makes them one-way.
(Also, they can't be "decrypted" by definition, since one-way
functions aren't ciphers and don't encrypt anything.)

The only way to recover the preimage of a one-way function from its
image is with additional information.  For example, with a crypto-
graphic hash that uses the MD construction (ie a block compression
function created by running a fixed-size bit-mixing function in some
simple chaining mode, with zero-padding for short blocks), then *if*
you know that the preimage is a single byte, you can brute-force it.
But that knowledge constitutes extra information.  Given only an
arbitrary hash value, there's no way to distinguish any of the
infinite number of possible preimages.  Even if the preimage is known
to be, say, exactly M bits long, M>N (where N is the output size of
the hash), there are ideally 2**(M-N) candidate preimages.

That said, if the preimage is short, and there's any reasonable
decision procedure for validating it, it can always be reconstructed
by brute force.  Choice of hashing algorithm makes no difference; an
attacker will simply ignore the hash value and brute-force the
original.  It's just a matter of the available computing resources.

We need a better set of requirements from the OP to propose a
suitable solution.  Perhaps simply zeroing out all the sensitive
information isn't suitable, for example, because the distribution of
values has to be preserved.

Note: I'll be on vacation next week and won't have access to Usenet,
so I won't be able to continue this discussion before Tuesday the
12th.
```

only because of the arcane system of rent-control laws.  Any 
Proper-Thinking Economist will tell you that when there isn't a law 
mandating a maximimum charge (x) for a limited commodity then the Free 
Market will set the price of said commodity lower (x-y, where both x and y 
are positive).

DD

## Thread: Find number of characters read with accept. — 9 msgs

_Topics: [`Language features and syntax`](topics.md#syntax)_

### Find number of characters read with accept.

- **From:** brian.joh@comcast.net
- **Date:** 2005-07-01T16:06:58-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1120259218.841793.237550@o13g2000cwo.googlegroups.com>`

```
I'm a COBOL newbie (just learned it today), but
I'm a pretty experienced programmer.

I wrote a very small COBOL program using
Microfocus Server Express 4 on Suse Linux.  The
program reads an ID and password from a user,
and then calls a C library (Kerberos) to
authenticate them to Active Directory
(authenticate them to a Windows environment).

I've got it working with one major hitch.
ACCEPT always pads strings with spaces, and
(AFAIK) there is basically no way to tell if
the user typed trailing spaces or ACCEPT put
them there.  That is, if the user enters
"ab12  ", I need to know that the user typed
those 2 spaces.  I cannot just strip off the
trailing spaces, because Active Directory
does not strip trailing spaces off passwords.
That is, "ab12  " is a valid SIX character
password in Active Directory.

I can read in the password from C, and I
will if I can't find a way to do this in
COBOL.  But it's much cleaner for us to do
this on the COBOL side. 

Any ideas?  Thanks!!!!
```

#### ↳ Re: Find number of characters read with accept.

- **From:** Russell <rws0203nospam@comcast.net>
- **Date:** 2005-07-01T22:54:23-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<Xns9686F3307C16rws0203comcastnet@216.196.97.131>`
- **References:** `<1120259218.841793.237550@o13g2000cwo.googlegroups.com>`

```
Try the "cursor is" syntax for the accept statement.
Note that the data name referenced in the "cursor is" 
syntax will need to be initialized to the start of the accept.

Your program will need to know where the accept is
supposed to be.







brian.joh@comcast.net wrote in news:1120259218.841793.237550
@o13g2000cwo.googlegroups.com:

> I'm a COBOL newbie (just learned it today), but
> I'm a pretty experienced programmer.
…[27 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

#### ↳ Re: Find number of characters read with accept.

- **From:** "Ron" <NoSpam@SpamSucks.Org>

- **Message-ID:** `<nZudnQLxz5Z3hVvfRVn_vg@giganews.com>`

```
How are you writing the ACCEPT?
I tried this with MicroFocus workbench and got
acceptable results but I don't if it is what you want.

01  input-area pic x(80) value low-values.
accept input-area at line 1.

When I typed 'ab12  ' I had
'ab12  ' with trailing low-values in input-area.
Exactly what the user typed including trailing spaces
followed by low-values (nulls) in the remainder of the field.

However, when I tried "accept from command-line" that
did indeed convert the trailing low-values to spaces. But
that form is used to pass line command parameters to
a program so that's probably not what you're doing.

Anyway, I'd be interested to hear how you resolve this.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Find number of characters read with accept.

- **From:** brian.joh@comcast.net
- **Date:** 2005-07-02T00:54:08-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1120290848.319650.324770@g14g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<1120259218.841793.237550@o13g2000cwo.googlegroups.com> <nZudnQLxz5Z3hVvfRVn_vg@giganews.com>`

```
This would be kinda painful, but I stumbled across another idea.
Read the data character by character, and keep reading until the
user types the return key.  Apparently, this can be done in
Compaq Cobol by putting the keyboard in auxilary mode and
using an "ACCEPT CONTROL KEY IN":

http://www.helsinki.fi/atk/unix/dec_manuals/cobv27ua/cobum_035.htm

Obviously, I need to do this in Microfocus, but I'm guessing
Microfocus can do something similar.
```

Hi,
  I'm using Visual Object COBOL Product Version 1.0.27

code of which is below;

       special-names.
       call-convention 74 is winapi.
       working-storage section.
       01 system-time.
           03 system-year                       pic 9(8) comp-5.
           03 system-month                      pic 9(8) comp-5.

       display "Day of week is:  " system-day-of-week
       display "Day of month is:  " system-day
       stop run.

"GetSystemTime" is, indeed, found in kernel32.lib. "GETSYSTEMTIME" is not 
found in kernel32.lib. I bet you've got the option to fold subprogram names 
to upper case turned on.

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Example of Calling a Win32 API Routine

- **From:** "jlcaverlyca@yahoo.ca" <jlcaverlyca@yahoo.ca>

$set SourceFormat"Free" Case

Joe

jlcaverlyca@yahoo.ca wrote:

> $set SourceFormat"Free" Case
> 
>   Not sure why this works, but it does.

The CASE directive ensures that the case of any external symbols is 
preserved. NOCASE will force all such symbols to upper-case.

SimonT.

## Thread: Visual Object Cobol dll and VB5 — 6 msgs

### Visual Object Cobol dll and VB5

- **From:** "jlcaverlyca@yahoo.ca" <jlcaverlyca@yahoo.ca>
- **Date:** 2005-07-03T10:09:13-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1120410553.157016.79550@z14g2000cwz.googlegroups.com>`

```
Hi,
  I'm using MicroFocus Visual Object Cobol Product Version 1.0.27 and
Visual Basic 5.0 SP3.

  After doing some Googling, I've created my first Cobol DLL, which I
have compiled, and have called from VB5.

  The Cobol DLL code is as follows;

       IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
       PROGRAM-ID. COBDLL.
       ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
       CONFIGURATION SECTION.
       SPECIAL-NAMES.
           CALL-CONVENTION 3 IS WINAPI.
       DATA DIVISION.
       WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
       LINKAGE SECTION.
      *
      * Short (Integer)  S9(4) Comp-5
      * Long  (Long)     S9(8) Comp-5
      *
       01  VB-SHORT      PIC S9(4) COMP-5.
       01  VB-LONG       PIC S9(8) COMP-5.
       01  VB-CHAR       PIC X(5).

       PROCEDURE DIVISION WINAPI.
       PROC-1.

           ENTRY "testcall" USING BY VALUE VB-SHORT
                                  BY VALUE VB-LONG
                                  BY REFERENCE VB-CHAR.

           IF VB-SHORT > VB-LONG
              MOVE "A > B"  TO VB-CHAR
              MOVE ZERO     TO RETURN-CODE
           ELSE
              MOVE "B > A"  TO VB-CHAR
              MOVE 1        TO RETURN-CODE
           END-IF

           EXIT PROGRAM.

My VB5 code is as follows;

Module1.bas:
Declare Sub TESTCALL Lib "cobdll.dll" _
  (VBShort As Integer, VBLong As Long, ByVal VBChar As String)

Form1.bas:
Private Sub Form_Load()
  Dim thestring As String * 5
  Dim num1 As Integer
  Dim num2 As Long
  num1 = 1
  num2 = 2
  TESTCALL num1, num2, thestring
  MsgBox thestring
  End
End Sub

A couple of questions.
First, I have to Declare the Sub as TESTCALL, as the DLL compiles this
as UpperCase. I found this out by doing a DUMPBIN on the DLL. How do I
make the DLL compile the Sub as testcall or TestCall?

Second, as I step through the code in VB5 after TESTCALL, num1 becomes
8258, num2 is 2, and thestring is still five spaces.

When I make num1 = 2 and num2 = 1, after TESTCALL num1 becomes 8258,
num2 is 1, and thestring is still five spaces.

I have a feeling that my problem may be in the CALL-CONVENTION, but I'm
not sure what to change it to.

Thanks in advance to anyone who knows what the problem is.

Joe
```

#### ↳ Re: Visual Object Cobol dll and VB5

- **From:** epc8@juno.com
- **Date:** 2005-07-03T12:37:09-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1120419429.890826.72280@z14g2000cwz.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<1120410553.157016.79550@z14g2000cwz.googlegroups.com>`

```
jlcaverlyca@yahoo.ca wrote:

> Hi,
>   I'm using MicroFocus Visual Object Cobol Product Version 1.0.27 and
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
>

> A couple of questions.
> First, I have to Declare the Sub as TESTCALL, as the DLL compiles this
> as UpperCase. I found this out by doing a DUMPBIN on the DLL. How do I
> make the DLL compile the Sub as testcall or TestCall?

1. Does the "case" directive you included in a recent post have any
effect on the symbols your program *exports*?

2. add an ALIAS "TESTCALL" to your declare, then you can call your Sub
whatever you want.

3. add a .def file to your build (somehow) which contains

EXPORTS
myname=TESTCALL


>
> Second, as I step through the code in VB5 after TESTCALL, num1 becomes
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Usually if your calling convention is off, you get a run time error
from VB. The calling convention must be stdcall for which WINAPI is an
older synonym. Passing the string from Basic ByVal looks right.

See http://supportline.microfocus.com/examplesandutilities/nesamp.asp

for some examples from NetExpress.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Visual Object Cobol dll and VB5

- **From:** "jlcaverlyca@yahoo.ca" <jlcaverlyca@yahoo.ca>
- **Date:** 2005-07-04T13:22:54-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1120508573.953149.256220@g47g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<1120419429.890826.72280@z14g2000cwz.googlegroups.com>`

```
epc8@juno.com wrote:
> 3. add a .def file to your build (somehow) which contains
>
> EXPORTS
> myname=TESTCALL

Hi,
  Just wanted to let you know that I looked into this.

  CBLLINK automatically creates a .DEF file for the build. After the
.DLL is created, it is automatically deleted, unless the switch is used
to keep it from being deleted, so that one can look at it.

  Nifty how things have become so automated since the 'old days'.

Thanks,

Joe
```

#### ↳ Re: Visual Object Cobol dll and VB5

- **From:** epc8@juno.com
- **Date:** 2005-07-03T16:24:38-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1120433078.266494.267080@g14g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<1120410553.157016.79550@z14g2000cwz.googlegroups.com>`

```
jlcaverlyca@yahoo.ca wrote:
> Hi,
>   I'm using MicroFocus Visual Object Cobol Product Version 1.0.27 and
…[58 more quoted lines elided]…
>

See my other message. This time I'm looking at your COBOL program in
more depth. VB passes arguments by reference unless you specify ByVal.
However, you do want to pass the string ByVal, otherwise you would pass
a pointer to a string descriptor instead of a pointer to the string.

On the COBOL side, I think changing your BY VALUE to BY REFERENCE for
the two integers might help.

Lastly, I'm not certain that your two COMP-5 items are really different
sizes. They might be. But if you really were passing them by value
before and your program did not crash, then I suspect that you were
really passing 3 4-byte arguments. VB is calling a subroutine in the
dll as if it takes 3 pointers.

[Sorry, I have not written any VB callable DLLs in COBOL, but I have
done so in a variety of other languages.]
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Visual Object Cobol dll and VB5

- **From:** "jlcaverlyca@yahoo.ca" <jlcaverlyca@yahoo.ca>
- **Date:** 2005-07-04T10:56:44-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1120499804.732265.239690@o13g2000cwo.googlegroups.com>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<1120433078.266494.267080@g14g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<1120410553.157016.79550@z14g2000cwz.googlegroups.com> <1120433078.266494.267080@g14g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`

```
epc8@juno.com wrote:
> See my other message. This time I'm looking at your COBOL program in
> more depth. VB passes arguments by reference unless you specify ByVal.
…[13 more quoted lines elided]…
> done so in a variety of other languages.]

I have changed my VB Declare to pass the numerics as ByVal. I have also
been looking at some of the other code on the net that has
"CALL-CONVENTION .. IS WINAPI. I noticed that alot of these were 74,
instead of the 3 that I was using. So, I changed it to 74.

I re-compiled the DLL, and it now works as it should. I changed the
values of num1 and num2 to make sure that "A > B" and "B > A" are
correctly displayed from VB.

I looked up in the VisOC help, and found "Call Conventions for
Interfacing with Mixed Languages", which breaks down how a call
convention number is determined. Here's how I interpret it;

1001010 - 74
||||||| Process parameters from right-to-left
||||||- Parameters removed from stack by called program
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
|------ The call conforms to the Windows stdcall calling convention

0000011 -  3
||||||| Process parameters from left-to-right
||||||- Parameters removed from stack by called program
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
|------ The call does not conform to the Windows stdcall calling
convention

I think that making the call conform to the Windows stdcall calling
convention may have had something to do with it.

Many thanks for your assistance.

Joe
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Visual Object Cobol dll and VB5

- **From:** epc8@juno.com
- **Date:** 2005-07-04T12:39:34-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1120505974.407478.7190@g47g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<1120410553.157016.79550@z14g2000cwz.googlegroups.com> <1120433078.266494.267080@g14g2000cwa.googlegroups.com> <1120499804.732265.239690@o13g2000cwo.googlegroups.com>`

```

jlcaverlyca@yahoo.ca wrote:
>
> I have changed my VB Declare to pass the numerics as ByVal. I have also
…[36 more quoted lines elided]…
> Joe

Confusion arose here because WINAPI has been used as a synonym for two
different things, convention 3 in 16 bit Windows (FAR PASCAL) and
convention 74 in 32 bit Windows (stdcall). Sorry I missed it earlier
:-(.

We can blame the C programmers for this one! Yes, with the right set of
header files, I can define a C function as being FAR PASCAL and it will
still compile and run on Windows XP.
```

<a id="t-296d75d73d"></a>
## Thread: flexible subroutine parameters — 10 msgs

### flexible subroutine parameters

- **From:** "Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com>
- **Date:** 2005-07-05T08:48:33-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3ivku2Fneup0U1@individual.net>`

```
I am trying to write a COBOL subroutine that will take some input and return
some output.  The input has some manditory and some optional parameters. 
Depending on the optional input some of the output may or may not be
created. 

I want to make the input and output flexible enough that I could add an
input option and/or an output field without requiring recompiling *all*
CALLING programs; specifically those that do not care about the new fields.

The CALLED subroutine will always be dynamically linked.

What would be the best way to do this that would allow me to not recompile
each caller but would also allow be to not read from or write over the
calling programs working-storage?

As an example, take the following copybooks:

* GETACCTI
01  GET-ACCT-INPUT.
    05  GAI-ACCT-NBR        PIC 9(9).
    05  GAI-NAME-ADDR-SW    PIC X.
        88  GET-NAME-ADDR       VALUE 'Y'.

* GETACCTO
01  GET-ACCT-OUTPUT.
    05  GAO-CURR-BAL        PIC 9(11)V99.
    05  GAO-AVAIL-BAL       PIC 9(11)V99.
    05  GAO-NAME-ADDR.
         10  GAI-NA         PIC X(40) OCCURS 5 TIMES.

ID DIVISION.
PROGRAM-ID. CALLTEST.
DATA DIVISION.
WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
01  GETACCT    PIC X(8) VALUE 'GETACCT'.
COPY GETACCTI.
COPY GETACCTO.
01  MORE-WORKING-STORAGE    PIC X(80).

PROCEDURE DIVISION.
    INITIALIZE GET-ACCT-INPUT
    MOVE 123456789 TO GAI-ACCT-NBR
    DISPLAY 'NAME/ADDR? ' UPON CONSOLE
    ACCEPT GAI-NAME-ADDR-SW FROM CONSOLE
    CALL GETACCT USING GET-ACCT-INPUT GET-ACCT-OUTPUT
    IF RETURN-CODE = ZERO
        DISPLAY GAO-CURR-BAL ' ' GAO-AVAIL-BAL
        IF GET-NAME-ADDR
            PERFORM VARYING SUB FROM 1 BY 1
              UNTIL SUB > 5
                IF GAO-NA (SUB) > SPACES
                    DISPLAY GAO-NA (SUB)
                END-IF
            END-PERFORM
        END-IF
    END-IF
    STOP RUN.

END PROGRAM CALLTEST.

ID DIVISION
PROGRAM-ID. GETACCT.
DATA DIVISION.
WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
COPY DMDMSTR.
COPY SAVMSTR.
01  AVAIL-BAL           PIC 9(11)V99.
01  NAME-ADDR               VALUE SPACES.
    05  NA              PIC X(40) OCCURS 5 TIMES.

LINKAGE SECTION.
COPY GETACCTI.
COPY GETACCTO.

PROCEDURE DIVISION USING GET-ACCT-INPUT GET-ACCT-OUTPUT.
    INITIALIZE GET-ACCT-OUTPUT
    PERFORM GET-DMDMSTR
    IF GET-SUCCESSFUL
        MOVE DMSTR-CURR-BAL TO GAI-CURR-BAL
        PERFORM CALC-AVAIL-BAL
        MOVE AVAIL-BAL TO GAI-AVAIL-BAL
        IF GET-NAME-ADDR
            PERFORM GET-DMSTR-NAME-ADDR
        END-IF
        MOVE ZERO TO RETURN-CODE
    ELSE
        MOVE 12 TO RETURN-CODE
    END-IF
    EXIT PROGRAM.

END PROGRAM GETACCT.

Now imagine that I want to add a new output field that is based on the
setting of a new input field.  Like this:

* GETACCTI
01  GET-ACCT-INPUT.
    05  GAI-ACCT-NBR        PIC 9(9).
    05  GAI-NAME-ADDR-SW    PIC X.
        88  GET-NAME-ADDR       VALUE 'Y'.
    05  GAI-CASH-RSRV-SW    PIC X.
        88  GET-CASH-RSRV       VALUE 'Y'.

* GETACCTO
01  GET-ACCT-OUTPUT.
    05  GAO-CURR-BAL        PIC 9(11)V99.
    05  GAO-AVAIL-BAL       PIC 9(11)V99.
    05  GAO-NAME-ADDR.
         10  GAI-NA         PIC X(40) OCCURS 5 TIMES.
    05  GAO-RSRV-INFO.
        10  GAO-RSRV-LIMIT  PIC 9(7).
        10  GAO-RSRV-BAL    PIC 9(7)V99.


If I changed the two copybooks but did not recompile CALLTEST then obviously
my attempt to read GAI-CASH-RSRV-SW would get me junk and writting to
GAO-RSRV-INFO would over-write CALLTESTs MORE-WORKING-STORAGE field.

Obviously I could do something like adding two length fields as part of the
parameter list.  But isn't there something simpler?  I tried declaring
GET-ACCT-INPUT and GET-ACCT-OUTPUT as EXTERNAL and not passing them as
parameters, but when I changed GETACCTI and GETACCTO and recompiled GETACCT
but not CALLTEST I got a run-time error that external storage length did not
match.  Which, of course, makes sense.  I was just hoping it might be extra
smart about this, but really I don't see how it could be.

Note, I do not have any access to OO COBOL, so while that would probably
make this quite simple, I have to do with standard ANSI 85/89 COBOL
(specifically COBOL for VSE/ESA).

Thanks!
Frank



--- 
Frank Swarbrick
Senior Developer/Analyst - Mainframe Applications
FirstBank Data Corporation - Lakewood, CO  USA

On Tue, 5 Jul 2005 08:48:33 -0600, "Frank Swarbrick"
<Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com> enlightened us:

>I am trying to write a COBOL subroutine that will take some input and return
>some output.  The input has some manditory and some optional parameters. 
…[136 more quoted lines elided]…
>FirstBank Data Corporation - Lakewood, CO  USA


The simplest way is to put a FILLER field of some length (maybe
X(100)) in the input and output copybooks.  Then as you need it,
redefine the FILLER.  Only those apps effected by the change would
need to recompile so long as you never exceed the initial FILLER
length.  Other apps would not have to do anything.

Regards,

          ////
         (o o)

be be sorry for tomorrow morning, sleep late."
-- Henry Youngman

#### ↳ Re: flexible subroutine parameters

- **From:** "HeyBub" <heybubNOSPAM@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2005-07-05T20:09:08-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<11cmbpi3ccshs23@news.supernews.com>`
- **References:** `<3ivku2Fneup0U1@individual.net>`

```
Frank Swarbrick wrote:
> I am trying to write a COBOL subroutine that will take some input and
> return some output.  The input has some manditory and some optional
…[132 more quoted lines elided]…
> Frank

When you CALL a subroutine, you do not pass parameters, you pass addresses 
to the parameters in the calling program. That is, the CALLING program 
passes ONE address for each parameter in the calling list. In your scenario, 
you may augment the copy books at will and, if the uncompiled calling 
programs never bump into the new fields, the old programs need not be 
recompiled or re-linked.

Specifically:
Pgm A.
01  Input-Group.
  02  Op-code   pic x.
  02  Input-A pic xxx.
01  Output-Group.
  02  Output-1  pic xxx.



Pgm B
01  Input-Group
  02  Op-code  pic x.
  02  Input-A pic xxx.
  02  Input-B pic xxx.
  02  Input-C pic xxx.
01  Output-Group.
  02  Output-1  pic xxx.
  02  Output-2  pic xxx.

In both Pgm A and Pgm B is found the statement:

  CALL 'SUBPGM' USING Input-Group Output-Group

It is up to SUBPGM to make sure it gets stuff from Input-Group and puts 
stuff in Output-Group properly, that is, according to Op-Code. For example, 
assume Pgm A processes Op-Codes "A" "B" and "C," each of which take as input 
a single value (Input-A) and return a single value (Output-1). Pgm A *MUST* 
only pass Op-Codes A, B, and C.

In Pgm B, however, can pass Op-Code "D" which takes THREE inputs and returns 
TWO results.

In developing Pgm B, you need not be concerned with anything associated with 
Pgm A save for the Op-Code idea.
```

Hi "Bub".  That sounds like a good idea.  I wouldn't use an OP code, per
say, but perhaps a "version" code.  So, in my above example (which I, of
course, deleted!) I would have

* GETACCTI
01  GET-ACCT-INPUT.
    05  GAI-VERSION         PIC 999 value 001.
    05  GAI-ACCT-NBR        PIC 9(9).
    05  GAI-NAME-ADDR-SW    PIC X.
        88  GET-NAME-ADDR       VALUE 'Y'.

* GETACCTO
01  GET-ACCT-OUTPUT.
    05  GAO-VERSION         PIC 999 value 001.
    05  GAO-CURR-BAL        PIC 9(11)V99.
    05  GAO-AVAIL-BAL       PIC 9(11)V99.
    05  GAO-NAME-ADDR.
         10  GAI-NA         PIC X(40) OCCURS 5 TIMES.

Then I could add new fields and handle it like this:

* GETACCTI
01  GET-ACCT-INPUT.
    05  GAI-VERSION         PIC 999 value 002.
    05  GAI-ACCT-NBR        PIC 9(9).
    05  GAI-NAME-ADDR-SW    PIC X.
        88  GET-NAME-ADDR       VALUE 'Y'.

* GETACCTO
01  GET-ACCT-OUTPUT.
    05  GAO-VERSION         PIC 999 value 002.
    05  GAO-CURR-BAL        PIC 9(11)V99.
    05  GAO-AVAIL-BAL       PIC 9(11)V99.
    05  GAO-NAME-ADDR.
         10  GAI-NA         PIC X(40) OCCURS 5 TIMES.

* GETACCTI
01  GET-ACCT-INPUT.
    05  GAI-VERSION         PIC 999 value 002.
    05  GAI-ACCT-NBR        PIC 9(9).
    05  GAI-NAME-ADDR-SW    PIC X.
        88  GET-NAME-ADDR       VALUE 'Y'.
    05  GAI-CASH-RSRV-SW    PIC X.
        88  GET-CASH-RSRV       VALUE 'Y'.

* GETACCTO
01  GET-ACCT-OUTPUT.
    05  GAO-VERSION         PIC 999 value 002.
    05  GAO-CURR-BAL        PIC 9(11)V99.
    05  GAO-AVAIL-BAL       PIC 9(11)V99.
    05  GAO-NAME-ADDR.
         10  GAI-NA         PIC X(40) OCCURS 5 TIMES.
    05  GAO-RSRV-INFO.
        10  GAO-RSRV-LIMIT  PIC 9(7).
        10  GAO-RSRV-BAL    PIC 9(7)V99.

Then I could do something like:
PROCEDURE DIVISION USING GET-ACCT-INPUT GET-ACCT-OUTPUT.
*   INPUT AND OUTPUT VERSIONS MUST MATCH
    IF GAI-VERSION NOT EQUAL TO GAO-VERSION
        MOVE 12 TO RETURN-CODE
        EXIT PROGRAM.
    PERFORM GET-DMDMSTR
    IF GET-SUCCESSFUL
        MOVE DMSTR-CURR-BAL TO GAI-CURR-BAL
        PERFORM CALC-AVAIL-BAL
        MOVE AVAIL-BAL TO GAI-AVAIL-BAL
        IF GET-NAME-ADDR
            PERFORM GET-DMSTR-NAME-ADDR
        END-IF
        MOVE ZERO TO RETURN-CODE
    ELSE
        MOVE 12 TO RETURN-CODE
    END-IF
    IF GAI-VERSION = 002 AND GET-CASH-RSRV
        PERFORM GET-DMDRSRV
        IF GET-SUCCESSFUL
            MOVE CASH-RSRV-LIMIT TO GAO-RSRV-LIMIT
            MOVE CASH-RSRV-BAL TO GAO-RSRV-BAL
        END-IF
    END-IF
    EXIT PROGRAM.

END PROGRAM GETACCT.



This looks like I great solution!  No programs would *need* to be
recompiled, but when they were recompiled they'd pick up the new version of
the copybook.

I have actually seen it used before, but I just didn't think of it.
Thanks a lot!

Frank

Frank Swarbrick
Senior Developer/Analyst - Mainframe Applications
FirstBank Data Corporation - Lakewood, CO  USA

I'm not up on VSE, but on z/OS you could pass each as a unique parameter 
and check the address of each linkage item for null upon entry to the 
subprogram.

E.G.

Procedure Division Using GET-ACCT-INPUT
                         GET-ACCT-OUTPUT
                         GET-ACCT-OUTPUT-NEW

   If address of GET-ACCT-OUTPUT-NEW not = null
      ...set some flags, move some fields, whatever...
   End-If

#### ↳ Re: flexible subroutine parameters

- **From:** jce <defaultuser@hotmail.com>
- **Date:** 2005-07-07T03:21:08+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<Xns968C39421967defaultuserhotmailco@65.32.5.122>`
- **References:** `<3ivku2Fneup0U1@individual.net>`

```
"Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com> wrote in
news:3ivku2Fneup0U1@individual.net: 

> I am trying to write a COBOL subroutine that will take some input and
> return some output.  The input has some manditory and some optional
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> new fields. 

Why is this such a problem? If your build member contained all the 
programs therein and you used a source tree management system then 
everything should take care of itself.
If you are in an organization that needs testing of everything to ensure 
integrity, then it's time to create a reusable test bed.

I'm personally not sure of having a program that you want to be a 
"common" module when it plainly is not a common module..if the outputs 
and the inputs vary you have something that's not common by my 
definition.  

In my opinion it's easier to maintain more than one program in the long 
run because it's absolutely clear as to the purpose of each module.  So 
if GETACCT did something you really wanted to keep common then re-call it 
from the "non common" version.

Original
CALL GETACCT using PARM1 PARM2

After adding something to the Input Output
CALL GETACCTA using PARM1A PARM2A 
    	where GETACCTA calls GETACCT using PARM1 PARM2

Having said that:

I think you wouldn't appear to be too poorly set with your "version" code 
and making sure that the linkage area is set to be the "largest" it need 
be as HeyBub suggested.


Stuff authored by:
> Frank Swarbrick
> Senior Developer/Analyst - Mainframe Applications
> FirstBank Data Corporation - Lakewood, CO  USA

##### ↳ ↳ Re: flexible subroutine parameters

- **From:** "Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com>
- **Date:** 2005-07-07T08:54:13-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3j4u0nFo3tcqU1@individual.net>`

```
jce<defaultuser@hotmail.com> 7/6/2005 9:21:08 PM >>>
>"Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com> wrote in
>news:3ivku2Fneup0U1@individual.net: 
…[38 more quoted lines elided]…
>be as HeyBub suggested.

Why do you say it's not a common module?  Basically, we have a demand
(checking account) and savings system.  They are separate databases and have
different structures.  My goal with GETACCT is that I can pass it an account
number and it will 1) determine if the account is on the demand system or
the savings system, 2) read the master account record for that system, 3)
populate a generalized "account information" structure.  This generalized
account info group can then be used by the calling program, and the calling
program doesn't have to care what "kind" of account it actually is.

As an example, in GETACCT we have something like:

EVALUATE TRUE
WHEN DDA-ACCT
    MOVE DDA-CURR-BAL TO GAO-CURRENT-BALANCE
    MOVE DDA-INT-ACCR TO GAO-ACCRUED-INTEREST
WHEN SAV-ACCT
  MOVE SAV-BAL-CURR TO GAO-CURRRENT-BALANCE
  MOVE SAV-ACCR-INT TO GAO-ACCRUED-INTEREST
END-EVALUATE

Now the calling program can simply use GAO-CURRENT-BALANCE and
GAO-ACCRUED-INTEREST and it does not care if the account was read from the
DDA database or from the SAV database.

The issue with the input and output copybooks being extendable is let's say,
for instance, that a program now wants to get the "interest paid last year"
fields, but I hadn't had the forethought to add this field to the original
copybook.  All of the other programs could not care less about this new
field, so I want to be able to add the new field to the GAO copybook but not
require all of the other programs (the ones that don't care about this
field) to be recompiled.

Do you still disagree with my doing this?

Frank


--- 
Frank Swarbrick
Senior Developer/Analyst - Mainframe Applications
FirstBank Data Corporation - Lakewood, CO  USA

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: flexible subroutine parameters

- **From:** "jce" <defaultuser@hotmail.com>
- **Date:** 2005-07-08T04:05:13+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<ZXmze.187821$IO.68888@tornado.tampabay.rr.com>`
- **References:** `<3ivku2Fneup0U1@individual.net> <Xns968C39421967defaultuserhotmailco@65.32.5.122> <3j4u0nFo3tcqU1@individual.net>`

```
Frank - reponses are posted throughout your response.

"Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com> wrote in message 
news:3j4u0nFo3tcqU1@individual.net...
> jce<defaultuser@hotmail.com> 7/6/2005 9:21:08 PM >>>
>>"Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com> wrote in
…[50 more quoted lines elided]…
> program doesn't have to care what "kind" of account it actually is.

In general I don't think the approach is the best to make - though arguments 
can sway me based on the number of times the "calling" modules are edited 
for other reasons (causing some concurrent development concerns).

If we take your approach you have one module - for the sake of simplicity we 
could provide it with a single input parm (say character 5000?) and a single 
output parm (say character 5000?) with one further condition that the first 
2 bytes of the input parm indicates "what the input and output struct is".

So now you have a calling program that you don't have to recompile - 
however, you also have a called program that needs to know how it's being 
called.  Why is this a better solution?

So this is contrived but it needs to be for you to understand my position 
(though ultimately, again, depending on circumstances, heybub's solution is 
perfectly adequate).  I will get around to why I think your solution is the 
best (with a twist) in the end for what you have:-)

> As an example, in GETACCT we have something like:
>
…[23 more quoted lines elided]…
> Do you still disagree with my doing this?

In MY opinion what you have now is two separate requests - get current 
balance and get paid interest.   As far as I am concerned you have 5+ 
options:

1. In your new module call one program to get the balance and another 
program to get the interest (NO recompile of old stuff)
2 .In your new module call one new program that gets interest (which in turn 
calls get balance for the balance portion)  (NO recompile of old stuff)

Now the advantages? You have very clearly defined what each function does - 
you do not need to read the code to know sometimes it does balance only, 
sometimes it does interest as well.  If for example you were calling the 
module - you'd have to look at both module each time to figure out which 
ones did what.

3. Make the parameters be "variable" and outputs "variable"
4. Recompile

If your program is truly common then all calling programs should get back 
accrued interest (none if there is none).  This means only a recompile - I 
find very few legitimate reasons why a recompile is a real issue...but a 
recompile makes the code very clear - I don't like explaining why I don't 
pass parameters, and what is the default anyway ? All of a sudden a calling 
program loses control of the called program.  By recompiling ANY program 
calling this module will get back both the balance and interest...and IT can 
determine whether the returns have value or meaning.

If you change the CALLED module, the fact that you don't change the CALLING 
module means that this will often NOT get retested with the new "default" 
parameters.  In a financial industry that's very risky - especially with a 
SOX (Sarbanes Oxley)  guy walking around.

5. Use static links - that way you will have the code appropriate to the 
link time
This is the worst as you would have to refer to the listing versus the 
source when reviewing.

There are 5 solutions here...you ruled out the last.  You started with the 
third.  I prefer the first and second...Only you know your environment.  The 
factors to consider are - how many recompiles are we talking? What is the 
quality of your test repeatability (the better the less intrusive a 
recompile but you should be testing anyway)? how often do you find the 
requirements for the "common module" to change ? How _many_ options will 
there be in that one module before you think it gets too much? How often is 
the called vs calling changed? How much employee turnover do you have? How 
good is the system documentation? Which is easier to figure out on short 
notice when you have a problem - the one with specific parms or the one that 
has "options"?

In short, 3 is acceptable to me, and in _your_ specific example might 
actually be the best solution but I wonder why you cannot just have a 
"rebuild all" function for your system.

What I would do based on your example is as follows (if I couldn't do 2):

Call GETACCT-INTERFACE  with INPUT OUTPUT where INPUT contains an ID "such 
as the calling program name" and the fields are passed by reference

In program GETACCT-INTERFACE set the addressability of the INPUT field to 
the appropriate Input Structure and call GET-ACCT-IMPLEMENTED
In program GETACCT-INTERFACE set the addressability of the OUTPUT field to 
the appropriate Output Structure and copy in the GET-ACCT-IMPLEMENTED 
results

This gives you your generic interface program and still keeps all the 
functions nice and tightly defined.  You could take advantage of a MOVE CORR 
if you really wanted to as this would appear to be one instance where that 
would work nicely without being _too_ abstract.

It would be nice if you had .NET versioning, and _REALLY_ nice if you had oo 
overloading though (in which case I would almost bet you that you would use 
option 2) :-)

My thing is that all code function be obvious.

JCE

>
> Frank
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> FirstBank Data Corporation - Lakewood, CO  USA
```

#### ↳ Re: Can't install Fujitsu Cobol v3 (student) in Win XP(sp2)!

- **From:** epc8@juno.com
- **Date:** 2005-07-05T15:23:53-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1120602233.887143.109260@z14g2000cwz.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<1120591726.688547.224940@g49g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`

```
montree wrote:
> I have tried to address the compatibity issue by running in win98 mode.
> And it says completed and needs to reboot the machine but I can't find
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> Steve

I was able to install this software on Win XP SP2 without difficulty
and without using any compatibility mode.

The package I used was COBOLV3.EXE obtained from Fujitsu's web site.

There was no request to reboot. After installation the programs reside
in c:\FSC\PCOBOL32. Installation creates an entry on the start menu
"Fujitsu COBOL 3.0". Try "Programming Staff".

This version does contain its own IDE, such as it is. You may find it
tolerable in time as I did eventually. One key point is that you have
to declare one program as the MAIN program. Google in this newsgroup
for more explicit directions.

Otherwise see:

http://www.adtools.com/student/index.htm

and

http://www.adtools.com/student/2000compatibility_tips.htm

Note that I have not used the software you eventually find by following
this link to Microsoft's web site. So beware!
```

## Thread: [NetCOBOL] Which key is invalid — 8 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers)_

### [NetCOBOL] Which key is invalid

- **From:** R.Hendriks@hotmail.com (RH)
- **Date:** 2005-07-07T01:38:48-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<fb1940e5.0507070038.7424f484@posting.google.com>`

```
LS,

I have a question on the INVALID KEY that is triggered and which key
triggered it. I have an indexed file (obviously) which has a primekey,
and an alternate key 'with no duplicates'. When writing a record, the
primekey may be invalid, the alternate key may be invalid (no
duplicates allowed!) or both.

The runtime nicely delivers the INVALID KEY mesasge but I have no
(known) way to determine which key is invalid. The file status is only
2 bytes and thus stores 23 and no futher info on which key. In
RM/COBOL there was a function for this (C$ERROR??) to get the deail
error info and thus which of the keys triggered 'invalid'. How can I
do this using NetCOBOL, any ideas?

Attention: I don't mean the contents of the key (which is still in the
FD or WS) but whether it's the prime of alternate key reporting the
error.

Using Fujitsu NetCOBOL v7 for Windows.

RH.
```

#### ↳ Re: [NetCOBOL] Which key is invalid

- **From:** "HeyBub" <heybubNOSPAM@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2005-07-07T09:35:39-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<11cqfdjidmsk47a@news.supernews.com>`
- **References:** `<fb1940e5.0507070038.7424f484@posting.google.com>`

```
RH wrote:
> LS,
>
…[19 more quoted lines elided]…
> RH.

I dunno. As a first approximation:

Close the file.
Open the (physical) file again with a different SELECT specifying WITH 
DUPLICATES on the alternate key.
Repeat the operation
If no error,
  1. It was the alternate key causing the problem.
  2. Clean up the mess
  3. Start over
  4. Handle the error
If error
  1. The primary key is the culprit
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Which key is invalid

- **From:** "Richard" <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>

##### ↳ ↳ Re: [NetCOBOL] Which key is invalid

- **From:** "Chuck Stevens" <charles.stevens@unisys.com>
- **Date:** 2005-07-07T14:40:05-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<dak7gd$20r7$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com>`
- **References:** `<fb1940e5.0507070038.7424f484@posting.google.com> <GWgze.62334$%Z2.31653@lakeread08>`

```
"John Simpson" <jasimp@earthlink.net> wrote in message
news:GWgze.62334$%Z2.31653@lakeread08...

>  Huh! File status 23 is 'record not found' at a failed read. It does not
> apply when writing a record.

From the viewpoint of standard COBOL, I think what applies to a write is I-O
Status 22:  "An attempt is made to write or rewrite a record that would
create a duplicate prime record key or a duplicate alternate record key
without the DUPLICATES phrase in an indexed file."  (ANSI X3.23-1985 page
IX-4; ISO/IEC 1989:2002 page 152 is similar).

Somebody might also encounter I-O Status 24:  "An attempt is made to write
beyond the externally-defined boundaries of an indexed file.  The
implementor specifies the manner in which these boundaries are defined."
(ibid.)   But I'm not convinced that the problem is the *key* in that
circumstance.

Other than these cases -- illegal duplicates, or attempt to write outside of
the file's boundaries -- I can't think of anything that might cause an
implementation to regard the contents of a primary or alternate record key
as encountered on a WRITE or REWRITE as "invalid" in the first place,
particularly since in '85 COBOL the keys are alphanumeric ('02 expands this
to include national).

    -Chuck Stevens
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: [NetCOBOL] Which key is invalid

- **From:** R.Hendriks@hotmail.com (RH)
- **Date:** 2005-07-07T23:20:14-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<fb1940e5.0507072220.7303b655@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<fb1940e5.0507070038.7424f484@posting.google.com> <GWgze.62334$%Z2.31653@lakeread08>`

#### ↳ Re: Which key is invalid

- **From:** "Robert Jones" <rjones0@hotmail.com>
- **Date:** 2005-07-08T03:02:43-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1120816963.270036.43490@g47g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<fb1940e5.0507070038.7424f484@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<fb1940e5.0507070038.7424f484@posting.google.com>`

```
When such an error occurs, try

1) reading the record using the primary key of the record you were
trying to write

2) reading the record using the alternate key

this is non-destructive to the file, so no tricky clean up should be
required and whichever was successful will indicate where the problem
is.

With regards, Robert
```

<a id="t-33b2538b0f"></a>
## Thread: MF: rebuild "in place"? — 2 msgs

### MF: rebuild "in place"?

- **From:** "Herwig Huener" <Herwig.Huener@fujitsu-siemens.com>
- **Date:** 2005-07-07T12:00:37+02:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<daiug5$hp4$1@nntp.fujitsu-siemens.com>`

```
2005-07-07 12:00:00 MEST

I find it difficult to interpret MicroFocus Documentation
for Server Express:

To my mind, the "rebuild" utility cannot rebuild an
ISAM-File where the data-file is damaged "in place"
- except for IDXFORMAT 8, where a special
command-line parameter can trigger this functionality.

As for own experiments, it was not possible indeed
to rebuild a damaged ISAM-file in place (IDXFORMAT 3),
whereas the rebuild into another file succeeded quite well.

However, a colleague of mine claims that a rebuild
"in place" should *always* be possible.

Who is right?

Herwig
```

#### ↳ Re: MF: rebuild "in place"?

- **From:** Russell <rws0203nospam@comcast.net>
- **Date:** 2005-07-07T08:04:51-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<Xns968C5C608693rws0203comcastnet@216.196.97.131>`
- **References:** `<daiug5$hp4$1@nntp.fujitsu-siemens.com>`

```
"Herwig Huener" <Herwig.Huener@fujitsu-siemens.com> wrote in news:daiug5
$hp4$1@nntp.fujitsu-siemens.com:

> 2005-07-07 12:00:00 MEST
> 
…[19 more quoted lines elided]…
> 
    	Ignoring any implications for "IDXFORMAT 3", rebuild in place 
assumes that the data portion is intact.  Rebuild into another file 
(note: REBUILD OLDNAME,NEWNAME) without the "/D" option assumes that both 
the data portion and index are intact.  To rebuild an indexed file with a 
corrupted data portion, you need the "/D" switch.  

    	I suppose you could rebuild in place, but the data would still be 
corrupted.  

    	Also note that when the index potion is excessively corrupted, you 
can help things along by replacing the index with a known good copy (even 
an empty one) BEFORE the rebuild in place or rebuild /D.  I have seen 
index files that were in such bad shape that rebuild could not figure out 
what the proper key strucure was.
```

idea how i can code<personlist . . .and<Person . .to generate a full 
xml-documentthank you very muchEinen schoenen TagAndreas Lerch

<refernce:myname> and any else.

#### ↳ Re: Cobol zOS 3.3 XML Generate

- **From:** "Richard" <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2005-07-11T12:58:13-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1121111893.630380.291660@g47g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<20050707.17573214@rechner12.lerch.xl>`
- **References:** `<20050707.17573214@rechner12.lerch.xl>`

```
> the XML GENERATE instruction

I had a look at Bill's reference and was not impressed by the way they
create XML.  Tying in the XML to the field names means that every minor
variation needs the program to be rewritten.  My approach to outputting
XML (or HTML or EDIFACT or printed forms or ...) is to use templates.
For XML there would be a text template giving the overall structures
required with tags indicating where the data items are to be inserted.
Repeat groups can be done using subsections or by having loop control
tags depending on how you like templating to be done.

A subprogram has to be written to do all the text processing and
substitution but once written can be used for almost any template.

:header
<personlist version="1.0" encoding="iso-273">
:person
   <person id="%id%" picture="%image%">
       <name>%name%</name>
   </person>
:trailer
   <total count="%number%" />
</personlist>

The program would have, say, a table of tag:value pairs that is passed
to the templating routine:

       move zero to tag-limit
       call template using "header" tag-limit tag-table
       read person-file next at end ...
        perform until pf-eof
           move 3 to tag-limit
           move "id"           to tag-name(1)
           move pf-code    to tag-text(1)
           move "name"     to tag-name(2)
           move pf-name   to tag-text(2)
           move "image"    to tag-name(3)
           move pf-picfile   to tag-text(3)
           add 1    to rec-count
           read person-file next at end ...
       end-perform
       move 3 to tag-limit
       move "number"           to tag-name(1)
       move rec-count          to tag-zzz9(1)
       call template using "trailer" tag-count tag-table

This way you can have alternate templates that output the same data as:
XML. HTML table, CSV file, printed form, EDIFACT, ... without changing
the program much.

The templating program can be made quite sophisticated. For example it
could have decisions:

?%image%:   <person id="%id%" picture="%image%">
!%image%:   <person id="%id%">

Where ? in col1 means 'if the tag's value is not blank' and ! means 'if
the tag value is blank'.

or

   <person id="%id%" picture="%image|default.jpg%">

where the bar starts a default value if the tag value is blank.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Cobol zOS 3.3 XML Generate

- **From:** "Richard" <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2005-07-11T13:33:25-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1121114005.420584.273590@f14g2000cwb.googlegroups.com>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<1121111893.630380.291660@g47g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<20050707.17573214@rechner12.lerch.xl> <1121111893.630380.291660@g47g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`

```
oops:
         ....
         perform until pf-eof
           move 3 to tag-limit
           move "id"           to tag-name(1)
           move pf-code    to tag-text(1)
           move "name"     to tag-name(2)
           move pf-name   to tag-text(2)
           move "image"    to tag-name(3)
           move pf-picfile   to tag-text(3)
           add 1    to rec-count

           call template using "person" tag-count tag-table

           read person-file next at end ...
       end-perform 
       ....
```

```
Jeff,

A lot of this depends on how you want the application to behave. From
the outline you have provided there are still many questions that
affect how I would approach this problem.

Just one of the things you should consider: how big are the tables, and
what would the impact of a join be? If you have 1,000,000 records in
table 1, and only 10% of them have the flag set to retreive data from
tables 2-4 then using a "joined" cursor would not be ideal here.

In the (rather large) application I develop here, I actually use both
methods you are describing depending on what the most practical is for
the task at hand. Joins can be a great asset when used in an
appropriate situation - but they can also be extremely detrimental if
you use then where they really don't "belong."

I know this isn't very helpful in addressing your exact situation, but
from the generalized post you've submitted its the best I can do for
now. There are a few of us here that have extensive experience working
with Pro*COBOL, so with more details about what you are trying to
accomplish, we may be able to offer better suggestions/tips.

Good luck.

Chris
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Are there any Pro*Cobol experts in here?

_(thread depth: 5)_

- **From:** "Chris" <ctaliercio@yahoo.com>
- **Date:** 2005-07-12T20:31:38-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1121225498.861525.56720@g14g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<1121192363.124150.36650@g14g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<1120833088.738122.62750@g14g2000cwa.googlegroups.com> <6tatc116brds1rgccsf2hqjbrqs8hqn97m@4ax.com> <1121081363.631987.175340@z14g2000cwz.googlegroups.com> <1121179644.124626.131020@g43g2000cwa.googlegroups.com> <1121192363.124150.36650@g14g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`

```
Jeff,

Based on what you are describing, I would attack this using a
combination of a "joined" cursor and a secondary cursor.

I would use a joined cursor between MEMBER and MBRSEPMSTR, since I
would assume that each member must have a name, and this relationship
is almost certainly going to be one to one and not one to many.

Then I would use a secondary cursor into DEMANDHIST or MEMBERHIST
depending on the value of demandacct returned by your "joined" cursor
above.

Unless you are calculating the SF-TOTREV field used in the sort
statement, you probably want to try and shift that sort to the cursor
declarations - since a) Oracle is much faster at sorting than the COBOL
sort verb and b) you can also create an index in Oracle that will make
the sort that much faster.

Again - this is speaking in generalizations - but I hope you get the
idea. If not I'm always available.

Good luck.

Chris
```

## Thread: Is it always possible to write a COBOL program using only 1 sentence per paragraph? — 186 msgs

_Topics: [`Language features and syntax`](topics.md#syntax)_

### Is it always possible to write a COBOL program using only 1 sentence per paragraph?

- **From:** "Oliver Wong" <owong@castortech.com>
- **Date:** 2005-07-11T15:41:16+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<wqwAe.115746$9A2.13677@edtnps89>`

```
    I'm trying to write a program that reformats the structure of a given 
COBOL program. One of the transformations I'd like to apply is to try to 
eliminate as many periods as possibles, using the END-whatever (END-IF, 
END-CALL, END-COMPUTE, etc.) constructs.

    My question is, is it always possible to do this? I don't want to 
"cheat" by adding new paragraph names at the beginning of every sentence 
(which may affect PERFORM statements anyway). My theory is that yes, it is 
always possible, but I haven't been programming in COBOL for that long, so I 
wasn't sure.

    - Oliver Wong
```

#### ↳ Re: Is it always possible to write a COBOL program using only 1 sentence per paragraph?

- **From:** Frederico Fonseca <real-email-in-msg-spam@email.com>
- **Date:** 2005-07-11T18:45:48+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<7ub5d1pej9vs5msg7v6mr9s6el06ah3kl5@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<wqwAe.115746$9A2.13677@edtnps89>`

```
On Mon, 11 Jul 2005 15:41:16 GMT, "Oliver Wong" <owong@castortech.com>
wrote:

>    I'm trying to write a program that reformats the structure of a given 
>COBOL program. One of the transformations I'd like to apply is to try to 
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
>
It is, but you need to have AT LEAST ONE period at the end of each
paragraph.

Some people will use a period on it's own, others will use a
"CONTINUE."

If you are going to do this (I don't agree with it myself) then I
advise you to use the "CONTINUE." way as it makes it very clear that
you have a "." there.





Frederico Fonseca
ema il: frederico_fonseca at syssoft-int.com
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Is it always possible to write a COBOL program using only 1 sentence per paragraph?

- **Date:** 2005-07-11T18:25:47+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<LQyAe.105291$HI.42516@edtnps84>`

#### ↳ Re: Is it always possible to write a COBOL program using only 1 sentence per paragraph?

- **From:** "Howard Brazee" <howard@brazee.net>
- **Date:** 2005-07-11T18:05:52+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<dauceb$qs1$1@peabody.colorado.edu>`
- **References:** `<wqwAe.115746$9A2.13677@edtnps89>`

```

On 11-Jul-2005, "Oliver Wong" <owong@castortech.com> wrote:

>     I'm trying to write a program that reformats the structure of a given
> COBOL program. One of the transformations I'd like to apply is to try to
> eliminate as many periods as possibles, using the END-whatever (END-IF,
> END-CALL, END-COMPUTE, etc.) constructs.

Why?

Is every statement that can use an END- clause going to have one?

>     My question is, is it always possible to do this? I don't want to
> "cheat" by adding new paragraph names at the beginning of every sentence
> (which may affect PERFORM statements anyway). My theory is that yes, it is
> always possible, but I haven't been programming in COBOL for that long, so I
> wasn't sure.

It's not possible to do this when not all of the code is visible.   If some of
the code comes from inaccessible copy members or from precompilers, then it
won't work.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Is it always possible to write a COBOL program using only 1 sentence per paragraph?

- **From:** "Oliver Wong" <owong@castortech.com>
- **Date:** 2005-07-11T18:35:57+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<h_yAe.105304$HI.45433@edtnps84>`
- **References:** `<wqwAe.115746$9A2.13677@edtnps89> <dauceb$qs1$1@peabody.colorado.edu>`

```
"Howard Brazee" <howard@brazee.net> wrote in message 
news:dauceb$qs1$1@peabody.colorado.edu...
>
> On 11-Jul-2005, "Oliver Wong" <owong@castortech.com> wrote:
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> Why?

Mainly to facilitate GOTO elimination. For example, given the code:

PROCEDURE DIVISION.
  IF A THEN
    DISPLAY "A"
    GO TO TERM-PROC
  END-IF
  DISPLAY "B".
  DISPLAY "C".
TERM-PROC.
  EXIT PROGRAM.

I'll first remove all the periods (that don't terminate a paragraph) to get

PROCEDURE DIVISION.
  IF A THEN
    DISPLAY "A"
    GO TO TERM-PROC
  END-IF
  DISPLAY "B"
  DISPLAY "C"
  .
TERM-PROC.
  EXIT PROGRAM
  .

and then I can transform it to:

PROCEDURE DIVISION.
  IF A THEN
    DISPLAY "A"
    SET GOTOFLAG TO TRUE
  END-IF
  IF GOTOFLAG IS FALSE THEN
    DISPLAY "B"
    DISPLAY "C"
  ENDIF
TERM-PROC.
  EXIT PROGRAM.

Whereas if 'DISPLAY "B"' and 'DISPLAY "C"' had periods after them, it would 
be more difficult for my code to group them together under the new IF THEN 
clause.

> Is every statement that can use an END- clause going to have one?

For simplicity, yes. The output isn't meant to be read by humans, but rather 
it's to serve as the input for yet more code manipulation algorithms.

>>     My question is, is it always possible to do this? I don't want to
>> "cheat" by adding new paragraph names at the beginning of every sentence
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> precompilers, then it won't work.

    Hmm, good point. I think my code can handle the COPY statements, but 
it'll probably break with in the presence of conditional compilation 
markers. Okay, thanks.

    - Oliver
```

```
Oliver Wong wrote:

>"Howard Brazee" <howard@brazee.net> wrote in message 
>news:dauceb$qs1$1@peabody.colorado.edu...
…[92 more quoted lines elided]…
>
Wouldn't you want to simply substitute something like:
IF A
    DISPLAY "A"
ELSE
    DISPLAY "B"
    DISPLAY "C"
END-IF
.
There is no need to introduce a variable, set it, and test it.  In my 
opinion, it doesn't "improve" the code; rather, it makes it even harder 
to understand.

After nearly 40 years of programming, and working on the programs of 
others, I can easily believe that you could find an example such as the 
one you cited.  They seem to be everywhere.  However, I would be equally 
unimpressed with the proposed "solution", because it takes what is 
"simple, bad" code and replaces it with "not as simple, still bad" code.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: About your example...

_(thread depth: 7)_

- **From:** Arnold Trembley <arnold.trembley@worldnet.att.net>
- **Date:** 2005-07-12T06:20:18+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<CiJAe.412583$cg1.88929@bgtnsc04-news.ops.worldnet.att.net>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<OoydnRb_uNAWuU7fRVn-vw@adelphia.com>`
- **References:** `<wqwAe.115746$9A2.13677@edtnps89> <h_yAe.105304$HI.45433@edtnps84> <TO2dnVxaoruLU0_fRVn-vw@adelphia.com> <AEAAe.105441$HI.1740@edtnps84> <dauqfd$bh$1@panix5.panix.com> <OoydnRb_uNAWuU7fRVn-vw@adelphia.com>`

```


Colin Campbell wrote:

> docdwarf@panix.com wrote:
> (snip)
…[13 more quoted lines elided]…
> Seems like there is very little "profit" in that....

Several years ago I used IBM's COBOL Structuring Facility to 
restructure several programs and move them into production.  I've told 
this story a few times before.  My company dropped the license for 
IBM-CSF because hardly anyone ever used it.

I found it to be a pretty impressive product, simply amazing that it 
could do what it did.  For really ugly spaghetti code it had to 
generate switches and branches to eliminate the worst cases of PERFROM 
THRU and ALTER.

On the plus side, it was 100% successful at eliminating GO TO, ALTER, 
and PERFROM THRU.  If you wanted it to generate SECTIONS with every 
SECTION having an EXIT, you could set it up to do that (and still get 
rid of every GO TO and ALTER).  I chose the option to generated 
paragraphs only, with no sections.  I never found any program bugs 
generated by the restructuring facility itself.  It would also 
reformat the code somewhat (consistent indentation of IF's, etc.) and 
optionally generate "called by" comments at the top of each output 
paragraph.  One of the surprises I found using it was the amount of 
dead code that could not be generated into the restructured program. 
I think it was carried over as commented-out code.  Getting rid of 
dead code could be a benefit, or an indication of just how poorly 
written the original program was.

On the down side, the generated program was a bit larger (all those 
"called by" comments), and had fewer paragraph names.  And if the 
original program had uninformative datanames and procedure names, they 
would still be meaningless in the generated program.  In my opinion, 
if you wanted a well-written program, then a programmer still had to 
modify the automatically restructured code.  But the tool saved you 
quite a bit of work getting rid of the spaghetti.

I still have one or two old programs in production that I would like 
to restructure if we still had a license for CSF.
```

```
Colin,

While it might be very satisfying to fix the last clunker in my 
inventory, I couldn't take you up on your very thoughtful and generous 
offer, for the obvious reasons.

And if it's not obvious to some of the readers here in 
comp.lang.cobol, companies frown on revealing source code to third 
parties, because the business rules in the source code are the 
intellectual property of the company.  They are trade secrets.  During 
the Y2K frenzy it was not too difficult to discuss problems with date 
routines, because those don't really reveal any business rules.

This is also why students rarely can find interesting COBOL source 
code on the net.  If it's a piece of code that has real value to a 
company, then it is not likely to be available for public viewing at 
no charge.

There are only two ways I can imagine that restructuring tools can be 
marketed for COBOL.  The first is as a tool that can be leased or 
purchased, so the user can fix their code and keep it private.  The 
second is probably as a fee for service arrangement, with contracts 
and confidentiality agreements.

In my 25 years of COBOL programming I can only remember one time when 
I was directed to send source code off-site to a third party (not 
counting certain programs we sell or give to customers so they can 
interface with our systems), and that was Y2K related.  We hired a 
third party to analyze a ton of COBOL source code to see if we had 
missed anything in our remediation.  The reports were impressive, and 
they confirmed we had done a very thorough job.  I wished we had such 
sophisticated tools.  But I believe that company went out of business 
shortly after the rollover.

If Oliver Wong can write a COBOL restructuring tool all by himself, I 
would say he must be one of the world's best programmers.  Even if he 
doesn't quite succeed, it's still an incredibly challenging learning 
experience.

While I would love to see a freeware or open-source COBOL 
restructuring tool, or even a low-priced one, I seriously doubt it 
will ever happen.  There needs to be a reasonable return for the 
investment of that much programming effort.

With kindest regards,

(Top post only)


Colin Campbell wrote:

> Arnold Trembley wrote:
> 
…[12 more quoted lines elided]…
> Colin
```

"Howard Brazee" <howard@brazee.net> wrote in message 
news:db0l8b$f2d$1@peabody.colorado.edu...
> Why do you suspect they might occur at least once?    I haven't seen one 
> in
> decades and they are no longer supported.

    The the majority of the test files aren't "real" COBOL programs that do 
anything "useful", but rather are intended to illustrate as many different 
"things" that a correct ANSI 85 COBOL compiler should be able to handle. At 
the very least, I'd expect each statement to appear at least once.

> Depending upon your employment status, and how likely you think they might 
> be,
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> needs isn't trivial.     Again - I haven't seen this in decades either.

    I've done some research on the semantics of independent segments in 
SECTION declarations, and this is one of the obstacles I cannot currently 
handle.

    The strategy we're using right now is "start with the easy cases, and 
work your way up". So right now I'm trying to eliminate COBOL programs with 
just a single GO TO, no ALTER or PERFORM/PERFORM THRU or segmentation or 
anything like that. Gotta be able to handle GO TO in IF statements, loops, 
EVALUATE statements, and all those fun cases. Luckily, unlike some other 
languages, it seems like in COBOL you can only use GO TO to jump out of 
these constructs, not into the constructs. Once I've got all those cases 
working, I can start worrying about PERFORM THRUs and ALTERs. And then from 
there, maybe it'll become more clear how to handle segmentation. Worst case, 
as you've said, is for the tool to simply detect segmentation and give up, 
reporting an error.

    - Oliver
```

Decide whether you want to eliminate SECTIONs and all drop through paragraphs.

Obviously you can't change one of these without affecting all programs that use
them.

that your "easy cases" fit into the big picture.

Does your new compiler have some of the very newest features such as EXIT

```

"Howard Brazee" <howard@brazee.net> wrote in message 
news:db0v8j$kkc$1@peabody.colorado.edu...
> My compiler is old enough that it does not support EXIT PERFORM (EXIT 
> PARAGRAPH
> and EXIT SECTION).   If yours has these ways to get out of a loop, you 
> will want
> to use them.

    Oh, yes, in that sense, I can indeed output code using the EXIT PERFORM 
statement. Thanks for the tip; it would have probably been very easy for me 
to go overboard with adding flags everywhere and forgetting about the 
existence of the EXIT PERFORM statement (indeed, one of the transformations 
I was planning on using does require a way to break out of loops).

>
> Hmmm.    Consider the following code and what you plan to do to it.
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
>      END-PERFORM.

    Okay, again this is just me as a human trying to mechanically apply the 
rules, but I think the transformation step will look like this (assuming no 
malicious ALTERs or anything like that elsewhere in the code):

PERFORM UNTIL A=B
  PERFORM GET-SALAD
  ADD 1 to A
  IF SALAD = GREEN
    SET SHOULD-GOTO-EXIT TO TRUE
    EXIT PERFORM
  END-IF
  PERFORM GET-DRESSING
END-PERFORM
IF SHOULD-GOTO-EXIT THEN
  GO TO EXIT
END-IF
.

Where the transformation of the last GOTO depends on whether EXIT appears 
above or below the GO TO.

    - Oliver
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: About your example...

_(thread depth: 13)_

- **From:** "Richard" <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2005-07-12T14:05:21-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1121202321.600314.214670@o13g2000cwo.googlegroups.com>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<kESAe.106846$HI.92351@edtnps84>`
- **References:** `<wqwAe.115746$9A2.13677@edtnps89> <h_yAe.105304$HI.45433@edtnps84> <TO2dnVxaoruLU0_fRVn-vw@adelphia.com> <AEAAe.105441$HI.1740@edtnps84> <dauqfd$bh$1@panix5.panix.com> <l0PAe.149449$on1.34681@clgrps13> <db0gss$cdl$1@peabody.colorado.edu> <aeQAe.106819$HI.4175@edtnps84> <db0l8b$f2d$1@peabody.colorado.edu> <%0RAe.106826$HI.106685@edtnps84> <db0p7f$hej$1@peabody.colorado.edu> <kESAe.106846$HI.92351@edtnps84>`

```
> will have to handle may contain the EXIT PARAGRAPH

EXIT PARAGRAPH and SECTION are works of the devil ;-)   In many ways
they have some of the problems of GO TO and NEXT SENTENCE.  As with
those they are 100% clear and definite abouut what happens when you
look at the words themselves, but cloak what happens when you are
examining the target point.

Or, specifically, if there are any of these anywhere in the program
then it is always necessary to examine every possible context on any
change.  If these are proven to not exist then the amount of context is
much reduced and productivity is much greater.

One of the ways that I simplify code is by breaking it down into
smaller paragraphs that are grouped.  For example if I find that nested
IFs are getting too deeply indented it is easy to rip out imperitive
statements into a paragraph and perform it.  EXIT ~ get in the way of
doing this, just as GO TO does.
```

> >
> > PROCEDURE DIVISION.
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
>
In my opinion this coding style is a lot more unstructured than the original
code !

I have also been coding Cobol for 20 years - and the problems with
unstructured programs are note GOTO's .. it's the lousy algorithms
underneath, it's the use of hopeless variable names, its the use to swicthes
or flags ... and like here the introduction of error possibilities .... if
yo just add another statement after the second end_if (saying the section is
a lot longer and more complex than here) ... then we have to have all that
inside the second IF ..... just because that we for some reason dont like a
GOTO to an exit :-)

The way that we always code is ... always have sections and paragraphs,
always perform, never ever perform though, always just GOTO's to exits or
top of a section.  Never sections bigger than 3 pages in your favorite
editor. + a couple of more items (no alter etc),

regards
Mette

```

"Mette Stephansen" <mm> wrote in message 
news:42d2d4e0$0$4723$edfadb0f@dread15.news.tele.dk...
> In my opinion this coding style is a lot more unstructured than the 
> original
…[12 more quoted lines elided]…
> GOTO to an exit :-)

    Yes, unfortunately because these transformations I want to do are going 
to be done by a computer, there'll be even more hopelessly meaningless 
variable names, and introductions of lots of falgs and switches. As I 
mentioned in another post though, the results of this transformation is not 
intended to be read by human programmers, but it's just there to make code 
analysis easier. Right now, all the algorithms I've seen for logic flow 
analysis and the such work a lot better if there are zero GO TO statements 
in the code.

    As for the possibility for introducing a new error, I won't have to 
worry about that too much, because all the modifications are going to be 
done by automatic tools. So assuming that I can prove all my transformations 
won't modify the semantics of the COBOL program, I know the tools will do 
the right thing. Actually, that's the reason I asked this question about 1 
sentence per paragraph in the first place; to make sure that my 
transformation won't change the behaviour of the program!

    - Oliver

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Is it always possible to write a COBOL program using only 1 sentence per paragraph?

- **From:** "Oliver Wong" <owong@castortech.com>

- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<PMAAe.105448$HI.43831@edtnps84>`
- **References:** `<wqwAe.115746$9A2.13677@edtnps89> <dauceb$qs1$1@peabody.colorado.edu> <h_yAe.105304$HI.45433@edtnps84> <dauj3r$1m2$1@peabody.colorado.edu>`

```
"Howard Brazee" <howard@brazee.net> wrote in message 
news:dauj3r$1m2$1@peabody.colorado.edu...
> I'm a big proponent of structured code.    But I would rather leave the GO 
> TO in
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> lot more than GO TO - less code.

    I understand your distate (I share it as well), so let's just say that 
"GO TO elimination" is a requirement for the project I'm working on. If the 
code is "easy to understand", that's a plus, but it a non-negotiable 
requirement for me that there be no GO TO statements.

> Does your restructure handle *real* spaghetti code?   With GO TOs pointing 
> all
> over the place?

    That's the plan. In theory, the algorithms should be able to handle 
everything (PERFORM THRUs, ALTERed GOTOs, fall through logic, the works) 
except for SECTIONS with independent overlayed segments (which is low 
priority because it doesn't seem to appear in any of my sample COBOL files, 
but still laying in the back of my mind as a future problem I'll have to 
eventually address).

    In practice, I've just started trying to implement the algorithms, and 
the first obstacle I've encountered is the desire to have just 1 sentence 
per paragraph to make the future transformations more easy. So I started to 
wonder if I could always transform a given COBOL program to an equivalent 
one with only 1 sentence per paragraph, and I couldn't think of a reason why 
not, but I thought I'd post on the newsgroup just in case.

    - Oliver

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Is it always possible to write a COBOL program using only 1 sentence per paragraph?
